| h₂erlf.J-on-eh₂- | - \\*h₂eCk'l-6n-eh₂-. The origin of the Verner alternation is unclear, as accentual mobility is unexpected in secondary eh₂-stems. It is possible, however, that the feminine developed from a neuter collective form \\*h₂eCk'l-on-eh₂- (cf. Lat. agna) created to the n-stem \\*h₂efk'l-on- as supported by Gr. CiKwv. It must then be assumed that the Verner alternation was adopted from this n-stem, which no doubt did have an accentually mobile paradigm. | tagra- | - \\*trahna- n. | tear | 544 | IE | \\*drli-h₂eli-ur/n- (IE) | pdf-text-headword-found |  |
| tahjansos | languages. The Germanic dialects provide evidence for four different stem variants: 1) Go. tagr, OE teagor < \\*tagra-; 2) OE t<Ehher, OFri. tar, OHG zahar < \\*tahra-; 3) MHG traher < \\*trahra-; and 4) OS, OHG trahan < \\*trahna-. Presumably, these variants all split off from a heteroclitic paradigm, e.g. nom. \\*tragru (> \\*tagru by dissimilation), gen. \\*trahnaz. According to Kortlandt 198Sb, the original PIE word developed from a compound \\*dr](-h₂e/(-ur, \\*drK-h₂eK-un-h₂, identifying the first member as the PIE root \\*der/(- 'to see' (cf. \\*turhta- 'clear'). The second element \\*h₂ek-ru- 'tear' can be retrieved from ToA ii.kiir, ToB akriina pl. 'tear', Skt. a§ru- n. 'id.', YAv. asrii n. pl.
